## INDIVIDUAL STOCK ANALYSES

### 1. CSL.AX (CSL Limited) -- Healthcare -- A$153.27

**Dip Analysis:** CSL has experienced a brutal ~35% selloff from its highs, driven by an 81% reported profit drop in H1 FY2026 due to $1.1B in impairments and $715M in restructuring charges related to the Seqirus vaccine spinoff (now postponed indefinitely) and a shock CEO departure. The underlying business grew revenue 4% and adjusted NPATA 7%, suggesting the headline profit collapse is largely non-recurring. However, structural headwinds persist: albumin sales in China down 27% on policy changes, CSL Behring revenue down 7%, and the US influenza market remains weak.

**Key Thesis Killer:** The Seqirus spinoff postponement removes the near-term value-unlocking catalyst. If China's albumin policy changes are permanent and US vaccination rates continue declining, the two largest headwinds become structural rather than cyclical. The 6.7% ROE is deeply below healthcare sector peers (15-20% typical), and even management's own projection only reaches ~17% ROE by FY28 -- still below the sector average growth rate of 20-24%.

**Verdict: Wait & See -- 45% confidence.** The dip contains real value destruction, not just sentiment. Wait for the first clean quarter under the new CEO, and for clarity on whether the $550M cost savings program is on track. The restructuring cloud needs to clear before this becomes actionable.

---

### 2. NAB.AX (National Australia Bank) -- Financial Services -- A$48.32

**Dip Analysis:** There is no dip here -- NAB just hit a record high on a Q1 profit beat (Feb 19, 2026). The RSI of 74.9 confirms the stock is overbought. NAB trades at a P/E of ~19.6x against a 3-year sector average of 16.1x, a 25% premium to its own historical average. Goldman Sachs initiated with a Sell rating, and Morgans has a price target of A$32.56, implying 33% downside. Pre-provision operating profit growth is projected at just ~1% per year through FY27.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Generational overvaluation. Australian banks are trading at PE multiples above pre-GFC levels with flat earnings growth. NAB's competitive pressure in personal banking and rising operating costs mean margins are compressing, not expanding. At 1% earnings growth, the current multiple has zero margin of safety.

**Verdict: Value Trap -- 70% confidence.** The stock is priced for perfection with earnings growing at 1%. Multiple analysts have Sell ratings. This is the opposite of a "buy the dip" candidate -- it is at the top, not the bottom. Avoid.

---

### 3. WBC.AX (Westpac) -- Financial Services -- A$42.54

**Dip Analysis:** Like NAB, Westpac is not dipping -- it is near highs with RSI 72.5. The stock trades at a P/E of ~22.2x, materially above the sector's 3-year average of 16.1x, and a 16% premium to its own historical average. Morningstar's discounted cash-flow fair value is roughly A$32.10, and consensus analyst target is A$33.70 -- both imply 20-25% downside. Zero analyst Buy ratings currently exist on the stock.

**Key Thesis Killer:** The home lending market is intensely competitive, squeezing margins. Net interest margin is already down to 1.94%. With zero Buy ratings and consensus at "Underperform," the market is pricing in growth that analysts universally doubt will materialize. Flat earnings with a contracting multiple is the base case.

**Verdict: Value Trap -- 72% confidence.** Trading at a DCF premium of 30%+ with zero Buy ratings from the street. The rally is sentiment-driven, not earnings-driven. Avoid.

---

### 4. ANZ.AX (ANZ Group) -- Financial Services -- A$40.70

**Dip Analysis:** ANZ is less overbought than NAB/WBC (RSI 67.4) but still elevated. The stock rallied 27% in 2025 and carries the same sector-wide overvaluation problem (industry P/E 21.2x vs 3-year average 16.1x). Unlike its peers, ANZ faces additional governance headwinds: A$250M in regulatory penalties across four cases, a new CEO executing a "cultural reset," and the ambitious "ANZ 2030" strategy that requires simultaneous turnaround execution and trust rebuilding.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Regulatory overhang is the differentiator. ANZ must run a turnaround and re-earn trust simultaneously -- historically a very difficult combination. The A$250M in penalties reflects systemic compliance failures, not one-off events. CET1 capital above 13% provides a buffer, but execution risk on costs, deposit mix, and digital investments is high.

**Verdict: Wait & See -- 50% confidence.** ANZ is the least overvalued of the Big 4 and has the most room for operational improvement, but the regulatory/governance risk is real. Wait for 2-3 clean quarters under the new strategy before considering. Would need RSI below 40 and a price closer to A$35 to be interesting.

---

### 5. MQG.AX (Macquarie Group) -- Financial Services -- A$219.39

**Dip Analysis:** Macquarie is at neutral RSI (58.7) and recently rose 2.4% on upbeat quarterly earnings. The stock trades at ~20x P/E and ~2x P/B -- rich but not extreme for a diversified financial with infrastructure and asset management exposure. The Qube acquisition (A$11.6B enterprise value) and Nomura asset sale (US$1.8B) are reshaping the earnings mix toward more stable, infrastructure-linked revenue. Revenue growth expected at 3.2% for FY26.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Declining commodities earnings, rising expenses, and falling ROE create a headwind that the Qube acquisition must offset. If the Qube deal faces regulatory delays or integration costs blow out, the investment thesis weakens materially. Additionally, MQG's earnings are inherently more volatile than the Big 4 banks, with significant exposure to market-sensitive income.

**Verdict: Wait & See -- 55% confidence.** Macquarie is the highest-quality name among the Australian financials here, with a genuine structural shift toward infrastructure earnings. However, the current price already reflects optimism. A pullback to A$195-200 or confirmation of Qube integration success would make this more compelling.

---

### 6. WDS.AX (Woodside Energy) -- Energy -- A$27.43

**Dip Analysis:** Woodside is overbought (RSI 73.7) near the top of its 52-week range (low A$18.61, high A$27.30). The rally is driven by Scarborough LNG project milestones and the floating production unit arriving on schedule. However, 2026 production guidance was lowered, and a planned Pluto LNG shutdown adds execution risk. Oil price forecasts point to softening in 2026 on ample supply.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Oil price headwinds. A Reuters poll predicts softer oil prices in 2026, and Woodside's near-term revenue is still overwhelmingly tied to commodity prices. The Scarborough LNG first gas is not expected until H2 2026, meaning the growth catalyst is still 6+ months away while the stock is already priced near its 52-week high. Lower 2026 production guidance + lower oil prices = potential earnings miss.

**Verdict: Wait & See -- 40% confidence.** Woodside's long-term LNG story is intact (50% production growth by 2032), but buying at RSI 73.7 near the 52-week high with softening oil prices and lowered production guidance is poor risk/reward timing. Wait for RSI below 45 and oil price stabilization.

---

### 7. FMG.AX (Fortescue Metals) -- Basic Materials -- A$20.04

**Dip Analysis:** Fortescue is the most interesting Australian name in this list -- RSI 34.5 indicates genuine weakness, and the stock is below analyst consensus targets. The dip is driven by iron ore price forecasts calling for declines to US$83/t by end-2026 (Westpac), China's PMI slipping back into contraction (49.3 in January), and structural decline in Chinese steel demand from the property sector crisis. However, Fortescue's C1 costs of US$17.5-18.5/wmt give it massive margin even at US$83 iron ore, and the company is diversifying into copper (Alta deal) and green iron.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Iron ore price trajectory. If iron ore drops below US$80/t on a sustained basis (not impossible given China property woes), Fortescue's earnings compress significantly despite low costs. The green hydrogen/iron pivot has consumed significant capital with uncertain returns, and analyst consensus is Neutral with a target around A$19 -- below the current price. The half-year results on Feb 25 will be critical.

**Verdict: Wait & See -- 55% confidence.** The cost structure provides a floor, but the iron ore super-cycle is clearly in its late stages. Wait for the Feb 25 results and monitor whether iron ore stabilizes above US$90. If both clear, the dividend yield at these levels could make FMG compelling. This is the closest to actionable among the Australian stocks.

---

### 8. INFY (Infosys) -- Technology -- $14.65

**Dip Analysis:** Infosys is in genuine distress -- RSI 33.1, with the NIFTY IT index down over 10.5% YTD in 2026 and the stock hitting a new 52-week low on Feb 13. The selloff is driven by sector-wide AI disruption fears (DeepSeek/ChatGPT threatening traditional IT services models), not Infosys-specific issues. The company's fundamentals remain solid: FY26 revenue guidance of 3.0-3.5% growth, over 90 generative AI programs in development, and integration of AI tools into service delivery. P/B exempt as a Technology stock, which is why it only missed RSI.

**Key Thesis Killer:** AI cannibalization of traditional IT services is the existential question. If AI tools reduce demand for manual coding, testing, and maintenance -- Infosys's bread and butter -- the entire business model faces secular decline. The current selloff reflects genuine uncertainty about whether Indian IT can transform fast enough to be an AI enabler rather than an AI victim. Revenue growth of 3-3.5% is anemic for a "technology" company.

**Verdict: Wait & See -- 60% confidence.** The selloff looks oversold on sentiment (AI panic) rather than fundamentals (Infosys is profitable, cash-generative, and adapting). Among Indian IT peers, Infosys has the strongest AI positioning with 90+ GenAI programs. However, the sector headwind is real and could persist for quarters. Would become an Asymmetric Opportunity if RSI drops below 30 with no further deterioration in guidance. Best Indian IT name to own if the sector stabilizes.

---

### 9. WIT (Wipro) -- Technology -- $2.26

**Dip Analysis:** Wipro shares the same AI-fear driven selloff as Infosys (RSI 32.6), but from a weaker competitive position. Q3 FY2026 showed some recovery signs: 1.4% sequential revenue growth, operating margins at 17.6% (best in 7 quarters), and $3.3B in total contract bookings. However, Q4 guidance of 0-2% sequential growth in constant currency signals the recovery is fragile. The Harman DTS acquisition adds engineering capabilities but dilutes margins.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Wipro has historically been the weakest of the top-tier Indian IT companies in terms of organic growth and client retention. The company's turnaround under successive CEOs has repeatedly disappointed. At $2.26, the stock is cheap on an absolute basis, but Wipro's structural competitive disadvantage vs. TCS, Infosys, and HCL makes the recovery story less credible. If AI disruption hits traditional IT services, Wipro is the most vulnerable of the Indian IT majors.

**Verdict: Wait & See -- 45% confidence.** If you want Indian IT exposure on the dip, Infosys is the better vehicle. Wipro trades at a discount for a reason -- weaker moat, weaker execution history, more vulnerable to AI disruption. The margin improvement is encouraging but not yet sustained enough to confirm a turnaround.

---

### 10. RDY (Dr. Reddy's Labs) -- Healthcare -- $14.49

**Dip Analysis:** Dr. Reddy's is not in a dip per se (RSI 64.3 is neutral), but the stock is trading at a compelling valuation relative to its transformation story. The company is pivoting from a traditional generics manufacturer to a diversified pharma platform with two major growth vectors: biosimilars (abatacept BLA submission targeted Dec 2025, launch potential 2027) and GLP-1 franchise (87 country launches planned in 2026, addressing an $80B+ global market). FY25 revenue grew 16.6% YoY with strong emerging markets (+32%) and India (+19%) offsetting North American generics decline (-16%).

**Key Thesis Killer:** North American generics pricing erosion is structural and ongoing (-16% YoY). If the biosimilar approvals face FDA delays or the GLP-1 launches encounter patent barriers from Novo Nordisk/Eli Lilly, the transformation thesis stalls. Tariff risk on Indian pharma exports to the US is a wildcard under the current administration. However, the risk is partially mitigated by geographic diversification (strong India/EM growth).

**Verdict: Asymmetric Opportunity -- 62% confidence.** Dr. Reddy's is the strongest candidate in this entire batch. The GLP-1 and biosimilar catalysts are concrete and near-term (2026-2027), the geographic diversification reduces US concentration risk, the valuation is reasonable relative to the growth pipeline, and the analyst consensus is "Strong Buy" with a $16.90 target (17% upside). The missed criterion (RSI 64.3) is trivially close to passing. Among healthcare peers, Dr. Reddy's has the most favorable risk/reward setup.

---

## SUMMARY RECOMMENDATIONS

**AVOID (Value Traps):**
- **NAB.AX** -- Record high, 25% premium to historical P/E, 1% earnings growth, Goldman Sell rating
- **WBC.AX** -- 30%+ above DCF fair value, zero Buy ratings, margin compression

**WATCHLIST (Wait & See, with triggers):**
- **FMG.AX** -- Watch Feb 25 results + iron ore above US$90; best risk/reward among Aussie names
- **INFY** -- Watch for RSI below 30 + stable guidance; best Indian IT name on AI dip
- **MQG.AX** -- Watch for pullback to A$195-200; highest quality Aussie financial
- **ANZ.AX** -- Watch for clean regulatory quarters; cheapest Big 4 bank
- **CSL.AX** -- Watch for first clean quarter under new CEO; restructuring noise must clear
- **WDS.AX** -- Wait for RSI reset + oil stabilization; Scarborough is H2 2026 catalyst
- **WIT** -- Inferior to INFY on same thesis; only if sector-wide recovery confirmed

**IF FORCED TO PICK ONE RIGHT NOW:**
**RDY (Dr. Reddy's Labs)** at $14.49 -- the only stock in this batch with concrete near-term catalysts (GLP-1 launches across 87 countries in 2026, biosimilar approvals in 2027), a "Strong Buy" analyst consensus, reasonable valuation, and a transformation story that actually has evidence of execution (16.6% revenue growth). The missed criterion (RSI 64.3) is not a red flag -- it simply means the stock has not yet pulled back, but it also has not run up to overbought territory. The asymmetry is in the pipeline optionality.

## Nordic Near-Miss Stress Test: Concise Assessment (Feb 21, 2026)

### Scorecard Summary

### Individual Stock Analysis

#### 1. ERIC-B.ST (Ericsson) -- SEK 102.05 | RSI 68.8

**Dip Analysis:** This is not a dip -- Ericsson has recovered strongly from its trough, with RSI at 68.8 approaching overbought territory. Q4 2025 showed solid results (SEK 12.7B adjusted EBITA, 18.3% margin, 9th consecutive quarter of margin expansion), and the stock has re-rated on improved profitability. However, the underlying RAN market remains flat in 2026, meaning growth must come from adjacent areas like enterprise and mission-critical networks.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Huawei has gained 2-3 percentage points of global market share since 2021 despite US sanctions, and Ericsson's CEO has openly warned about losing deals in Europe and Latin America to aggressive Chinese pricing. The EU proposal to mandate Huawei removal within 3 years is a potential tailwind, but execution risk is high and timeline uncertain. At a trailing P/E of ~12.7x vs Nokia at ~36x, Ericsson is the cheaper play, but a flat-to-declining TAM limits re-rating potential.

**Verdict: Wait & See (55%)** -- Valuation is reasonable vs. peers, but no catalysts for a breakout. Wait for a pullback toward SEK 85-90 or confirmation of EU Huawei ban implementation.

---

#### 2. INVE-B.ST (Investor AB) -- SEK 368.00 | RSI 71.3

**Dip Analysis:** There is no dip here whatsoever. INVE-B.ST is trading at SEK 368, at the very top of its 52-week range (247-366.4), with RSI at 71.3 -- firmly in overbought territory. The stock is at an all-time high, reflecting strong NAV growth driven by portfolio companies (AstraZeneca, Atlas Copco, Saab all performing well). NAV was SEK 336/share at Q4 2025, meaning the stock trades at a ~9.5% premium to NAV.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Investor AB historically trades at a discount to NAV, and the current premium positioning is historically unusual. Analysts recommend waiting for a deeper discount (ideally 15%+ discount to NAV) before buying. You are paying above liquidation value for a holding company, which violates the core value investing thesis.

**Verdict: Wait & See (40%)** -- Excellent company, terrible entry point. The overbought RSI and premium-to-NAV valuation make this a "buy the portfolio companies directly" situation. Wait for a broad market selloff to bring this back to a 10-15% NAV discount.

---

#### 3. SEB-A.ST (SEB) -- SEK 196.00 | RSI 51.7

**Dip Analysis:** SEB is range-bound, with RSI at a neutral 51.7 -- neither oversold nor overbought. This is not a dip but rather a stock in consolidation after a strong 2024-2025 run driven by higher interest rates. With the Riksbank holding steady at 1.75% and expected to remain flat through 2026, net interest income (the primary earnings driver) has plateaued. SEB's forward P/E of ~11.3x is slightly above the European bank average of 9.8x.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Earnings growth is forecast at a paltry 0.9% per annum, with EPS growth of 3.4%. The 2026 cost target of SEK 33.4B suggests the bank is in efficiency mode, not growth mode. Analyst consensus target of SEK 175.93 is actually 10% below the current price, indicating potential overvaluation at current levels.

**Verdict: Wait & See (50%)** -- Solid bank, but analyst consensus says it is overvalued at SEK 196. The rate cycle has peaked, limiting NII upside. Wait for a pullback to SEK 170-175 range for a better entry.

---

#### 4. SWED-A.ST (Swedbank) -- SEK 348.70 | RSI 54.1

**Dip Analysis:** Similar to SEB, Swedbank is in neutral territory with RSI 54.1. Q4 2025 was a strong beat (net profit SEK 8.17B, 13% above expectations, EPS 7.22), but the stock has already priced in the good news. The bank is investing in AI and digitalization with a 3% cost growth target for 2026 -- disciplined but not exciting. Baltic operations remain a growth pocket, but Sweden's housing market recovery is slow.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Like all Swedish banks, Swedbank faces a NII ceiling at the current Riksbank rate of 1.75%. Further rate cuts (which some analysts expect in late 2026/2027) would directly compress margins. Swedbank's heavy mortgage exposure in Sweden makes it more rate-sensitive than SEB's corporate-weighted book.

**Verdict: Wait & See (50%)** -- Better Q4 execution than SEB, but same structural headwinds. The 3% cost growth target and AI investment narrative provide modest differentiation, but not enough to overcome the rate environment. Between SEB and Swedbank, Swedbank has slightly better momentum, but neither is a compelling buy at current levels.

---

#### 5. EQNR.OL (Equinor) -- NOK 273.70 | RSI 63.0

**Dip Analysis:** Not a dip -- Equinor is trading near the middle of its range with RSI 63.0. Q4 2025 was a beat (adjusted EPS $0.81 vs. $0.61 expected), driven by record production from Johan Castberg and Halten East. However, the $4B capex reduction for 2026-27 is a signal that management is prioritizing capital returns over growth, particularly cutting the Power and Low Carbon Solutions segment. Production growth of ~3% in 2026 is modest.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Oil price risk remains the dominant factor. Equinor's 2026 cash flow projections assume flat prices; Brent below $65 would meaningfully compress returns. The capex cut in renewables signals a strategic retreat from the energy transition theme, which could alienate ESG-focused institutional investors. Forward P/E of ~11x is reasonable for an integrated, but there is limited re-rating catalyst unless oil spikes.

**Verdict: Wait & See (55%)** -- Solid operator with strong shareholder returns (4.26% yield + buybacks), but you are essentially making an oil price bet. At NOK 273.70, the risk/reward is balanced, not asymmetric. A pullback to NOK 240-250 on any oil price weakness would create a better entry for the dividend-and-buyback thesis.

---

#### 6. DNB.OL (DNB Bank) -- NOK 305.10 | RSI 68.9

**Dip Analysis:** Emphatically not a dip. DNB has surged post-Q4 earnings, with RSI at 68.9 near overbought. Q4 2025 was excellent (profit NOK 11.6B, ROE 16.6%, EPS NOK 7.65), and the dividend was raised to NOK 18/share. The stock has run hard on the back of a 40% jump in commissions revenue and wealth management growth. However, the analyst consensus target of NOK 287.75 is actually below the current price of NOK 305.10.

**Key Thesis Killer:** The stock is trading 6% above the average analyst target. DNB's P/E of ~9.45x is in line with the Norwegian bank industry average of 9.0x, so there is no deep value discount. The earnings beat has been fully priced in; any disappointment in Q1 2026 or a dovish shift from Norges Bank would create downside risk from these elevated levels.

**Verdict: Wait & See (45%)** -- Great bank, but you've missed the move. Trading above analyst consensus targets with near-overbought RSI is the opposite of "buying the dip." Wait for a correction to NOK 270-280, which would restore the value case.

---

#### 7. MOWI.OL (Mowi) -- NOK 232.60 | RSI 62.4

**Dip Analysis:** Mowi is recovering from a period of depressed salmon prices caused by exceptional 12% industry supply growth in 2025. Despite price headwinds, the company posted record revenues (EUR 1.59B in Q4) and record harvest volumes (559,000 tonnes for FY2025). Blended farming costs fell to EUR 5.36/kg from EUR 5.69/kg, demonstrating genuine operational improvement rather than just price-driven earnings. The RSI at 62.4 is rising but not yet overbought.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Norway's 25% resource rent tax (on top of 22% corporate tax, effective marginal rate of 47%) permanently impairs the earnings power of Norwegian-based salmon operations, which account for 80% of Mowi's earnings. This structural drag limits the upside even in favorable salmon price environments.

**Verdict: Asymmetric Opportunity (65%)** -- The combination of factors tips this positive: Mowi expects 605,000 tonnes in 2026 (8.3% growth vs. 1% industry growth), suggesting massive market share gains. Berenberg upgraded to Buy, expecting EBIT to more than double in 2026 as salmon prices normalize upward. Cost discipline is proven. The resource rent tax is a known headwind, already priced in. At current levels, you are buying the world's largest salmon producer at trough-to-recovery earnings with volume growth far exceeding peers (SalMar, Leroy). The risk/reward is skewed favorably.

---

#### 8. YAR.OL (Yara International) -- NOK 467.80 | RSI 66.9

**Dip Analysis:** Yara is in the midst of a powerful earnings recovery -- FY2025 net income surged to $1.37B from just $15M in 2024, and ROIC jumped from 0.5% to 11.4%. Q4 2025 EBITDA rose 37% year-over-year, driven by volume/mix improvements, higher margins, and $200M in fixed cost reductions. This is a cyclical recovery story, not a dip, and the question is whether the recovery has further legs.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Fertilizer is inherently cyclical and gas-cost-sensitive. European gas prices remain elevated vs. US peers (CF Industries, Nutrien), giving Yara a structural cost disadvantage in nitrogen production. Any spike in European gas prices (geopolitical risk, cold winter) would directly compress margins. CF Industries trades at ~9.3x P/E vs. Yara's likely mid-teens P/E, reflecting this structural cost gap.

**Verdict: Asymmetric Opportunity (60%)** -- The case rests on: (1) The $200M cost reduction program demonstrating management execution, (2) ROIC improvement from 0.5% to 11.4% showing the business model works when fertilizer markets cooperate, (3) The upcoming Capital Markets Day 2026 focused on "driving resilient earnings toward 2030" could serve as a catalyst, and (4) The proposed NOK 22/share dividend provides income while waiting. The risk is that this is a mid-cycle peak, not the start of a structural re-rating. But with the cost transformation story still early innings and fertilizer demand structurally supported by global food security needs, the odds favor continued improvement.

---

### Portfolio-Level Takeaways

**AVOID entering now (overvalued or overbought):**
- **INVE-B.ST** -- Premium to NAV, overbought RSI 71.3, worst entry timing
- **DNB.OL** -- Trading above analyst targets post-earnings, RSI 68.9

**WATCHLIST (wait for better entry):**
- **ERIC-B.ST** -- Good value vs. Nokia, but wait for SEK 85-90 pullback or EU Huawei ban confirmation
- **SEB-A.ST / SWED-A.ST** -- Rate ceiling limits upside; wait for SEK 170-175 (SEB) or material rate cut catalyst
- **EQNR.OL** -- Solid dividend play, but wait for oil price weakness to buy at NOK 240-250

**ACTIONABLE (asymmetric risk/reward):**
- **MOWI.OL** -- Best risk/reward of the group. Volume growth 8x industry average, cost discipline proven, Berenberg upgrade, recovering salmon prices. The resource rent tax is the known headwind but is priced in.
- **YAR.OL** -- Cyclical recovery with execution proof ($200M cost cuts, ROIC 0.5% to 11.4%). More volatile than Mowi but higher upside if fertilizer cycle extends.

**If forced to pick one right now:** **MOWI.OL** at NOK 232.60. The combination of structural volume growth (605K tonnes, 8.3% growth vs. 1% industry), proven cost reduction, and a recovering price environment creates genuine asymmetry. The resource rent tax is painful but known and discounted.

## Individual Stock Analysis

### SPANISH STOCKS

#### 1. SAN.MC -- Banco Santander (EUR 10.76) | **Wait & See -- 45%**

**Dip Analysis:** There is no dip here -- Santander is up ~120% over the past year and just posted record 2025 net income of EUR 14.1B (+12% YoY) with 16.3% RoTE. The stock is trading at ~12x trailing P/E and 1.4x P/B, which is a substantial premium to the European bank historical range of 6.8-8.1x earnings. The RSI at 55.8 is neutral, confirming this is a momentum stock, not a dip.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Valuation compression risk. If the P/E reverts from 12x to the 8x historical norm for European banks, the stock falls ~33% even with flat earnings. The 2026 mid-single-digit revenue growth target is modest and already priced in.

**Verdict: Wait & See (45%)** -- Record profits are real, but the risk/reward at these multiples is unfavorable. Wait for a pullback to the 8-9x P/E range.

---

#### 2. BBVA.MC -- BBVA (EUR 19.85) | **Wait & See -- 55%**

**Dip Analysis:** BBVA is not in a dip -- it has rallied 34% since the failed Sabadell takeover in October 2025, and is near its all-time high. Q4 2025 net profit rose 4.1% with strong performance in Spain and Mexico. The stock announced a record EUR 3.96B buyback. At RSI 44.7, it has pulled back slightly from peaks, creating a modest entry window vs. peers.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Capital allocation uncertainty. The failed EUR 17B Sabadell bid consumed management bandwidth for over a year. With nearly EUR 4B now going to buybacks instead, the question is whether BBVA has a credible inorganic growth story or just becomes a yield play.

**Verdict: Wait & See (55%)** -- Better positioned than Santander on valuation, and the Mexico franchise is a genuine differentiator. But at ~19.85 it is still pricing in a lot of good news. A dip below EUR 17 would be compelling.

---

#### 3. IBE.MC -- Iberdrola (EUR 19.76) | **Wait & See -- 50%**

**Dip Analysis:** No dip -- Iberdrola is up 50% over the past 12 months and just raised 2026 guidance to double-digit adjusted net income growth (above EUR 6.2B). Record gross investments of EUR 9B in 9M 2025, focused on regulated networks. The RSI at 63.5 is elevated but not overbought, suggesting continued momentum.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Valuation is stretched for a utility. Analyst targets range EUR 21.83-26.67, but at EUR 19.76 much of the upside is already captured. Regulated utility earnings should command a premium, but the 50% rally in one year means any disappointment in capex returns or interest rate reversal could trigger a sharp de-rating.

**Verdict: Wait & See (50%)** -- Excellent business, wrong price. Iberdrola's regulated asset base and renewable leadership are best-in-class among European utilities, but entry at current levels offers limited margin of safety.

---

#### 4. REP.MC -- Repsol (EUR 18.30) | **Asymmetric Opportunity -- 60%**

**Dip Analysis:** Repsol's 2025 adjusted net income fell 15% to EUR 2.6B on lower oil prices, yet cash flow from operations grew 8% to EUR 5.4B, showing operational resilience. At a ~6.6% dividend yield with the 2026 payout rising to EUR 1.05/share, and a planned upstream IPO as a potential value-unlock catalyst, the stock trades below consensus analyst targets (~EUR 16.72 avg, though the stock is at EUR 18.30 suggesting recent momentum). RSI at 71.9 is overbought short-term but the structural story is sound.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Brent below $60/bbl sustained would break the model. Repsol's own 2026 guidance assumes $60-65 Brent, which is already conservative. But a global recession scenario pushing oil sub-$55 would compress free cash flow and threaten the dividend.

**Verdict: Asymmetric Opportunity (60%)** -- The 6.6% yield provides a cash-flow floor, the upstream IPO/spin-off is a genuine catalyst, and the energy transition capex (35%+ of investment to renewables) provides optionality. The RSI overbought reading means patience for a 5-10% pullback would improve the entry, but the fundamental case is the best among the Spanish names.

---

#### 5. CABK.MC -- CaixaBank (EUR 10.97) | **Wait & See -- 50%**

**Dip Analysis:** CaixaBank hit an all-time high of EUR 11.575 on Feb 4, 2026 and has pulled back marginally. Q4 net income of EUR 1.49B was steady, and analyst targets cluster around EUR 11.10-12.50. The stock has been a direct beneficiary of higher ECB rates boosting net interest margins.

**Key Thesis Killer:** ECB rate normalization. CaixaBank is the most NIM-sensitive of the Spanish banks due to its heavy domestic mortgage book. As the ECB continues cutting rates, NIM compression will pressure earnings even if loan volumes grow.

**Verdict: Wait & See (50%)** -- Fairly valued at current levels. The domestic Spanish franchise is strong, but the rate sensitivity is a headwind in 2026. Prefer entry below EUR 10 where the yield becomes more protective.

---

### ITALIAN STOCKS

#### 6. ISP.MI -- Intesa Sanpaolo (EUR 5.87) | **Asymmetric Opportunity -- 65%**

**Dip Analysis:** Intesa posted record 2025 net income of EUR 9.3B with a new business plan targeting EUR 10B in 2026 and EUR 11.5B by 2029. RoTE above 20% and a cost-income ratio at 37% are best-in-class for European banking. The 95% total payout ratio (75% cash dividend + 20% buyback) is extraordinary capital return. RSI at 50.5 is perfectly neutral -- this is a rare case of a quality bank that is neither overbought nor oversold.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Italian sovereign debt crisis. As one of the largest holders of Italian BTPs, any sovereign spread widening would directly hit Intesa's equity through mark-to-market losses, even though the operating business remains robust.

**Verdict: Asymmetric Opportunity (65%)** -- The highest-conviction name in this entire list. Record profitability, massive capital returns, neutral RSI, and analyst targets of EUR 6.45-7.20 imply 10-23% upside. The sovereign risk is real but structurally mitigated by ECB backstops. Among European bank peers, Intesa offers the best combination of quality, valuation, and shareholder return.

---

#### 7. UCG.MI -- UniCredit (EUR 73.93) | **Wait & See -- 55%**

**Dip Analysis:** UniCredit posted record 2025 net profit of EUR 10.6B (+14% YoY) with 19.2% RoTE and EUR 9.5B in shareholder distributions. The stock has tripled from the low EUR 20s in early 2024. At RSI 52.3, momentum is neutral. The Banco BPM bid withdrawal and Commerzbank overhang have been resolved as negatives, freeing capital.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Dual regulatory risk. UniCredit holds ~21% of Commerzbank through derivatives expiring in 2026 -- the resolution (sell, hold, or acquire) creates binary outcome risk. Separately, Italian golden power restrictions cited Russia exposure as a concern, and any escalation of Russia-related sanctions could force balance sheet charges.

**Verdict: Wait & See (55%)** -- Excellent fundamentals but too many unresolved strategic wildcards. The Commerzbank position must be resolved in 2026, creating an event-driven opportunity but also risk. Wait for clarity on the Commerzbank decision before entering.

---

#### 8. G.MI -- Assicurazioni Generali (EUR 35.68) | **Wait & See -- 45%**

**Dip Analysis:** Generali has rallied from EUR 20.83 to EUR 35.68 over two years, driven by improved operational efficiency and capital return. Analyst consensus is Moderate Buy with targets around EUR 36.50-38.50, implying modest 2-8% upside. RSI at 58.3 is mildly elevated.

**Key Thesis Killer:** The collapse of the Natixis Investment Management JV removes Generali's most significant growth catalyst. The deal, which would have created Europe's largest asset manager by revenue with EUR 1.9T AUM, was killed by Italian government opposition. Without this, Generali's growth story reverts to slow organic insurance income growth.

**Verdict: Wait & See (45%)** -- A solid insurance franchise trading near fair value, but the Natixis JV failure materially weakens the medium-term growth narrative. Limited upside at current prices with the primary catalyst removed.

---

### CANADIAN STOCKS

#### 9. RY.TO -- Royal Bank of Canada (CAD 236.00) | **Wait & See -- 50%**

**Dip Analysis:** RBC reports Q1 2026 on Feb 26 with consensus expecting C$2.76 EPS (+8.2% YoY) on C$12.1B revenue. The HSBC Canada integration is accretive, the dividend was hiked 6.5% to C$1.64/quarter, and the ROE target was raised to 17%+. At RSI 59.8, it is modestly elevated. The stock trades at a premium to Canadian bank peers, reflecting its dominant market position.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Premium valuation leaves no room for error. RBC already trades at the richest multiples among Canadian Big 6 banks. With C$324B market cap, meaningful upside requires revenue acceleration beyond the mid-single-digit range, which is unlikely in a slowing Canadian housing market.

**Verdict: Wait & See (50%)** -- Best-in-class franchise, but priced accordingly. The HSBC integration tailwind is fully discounted. Prefer to own on a 10-15% pullback.

---

#### 10. TD.TO -- Toronto-Dominion Bank (CAD 132.79) | **Asymmetric Opportunity -- 60%**

**Dip Analysis:** TD is the most contrarian play among Canadian banks. Despite a 65.85% YoY share price surge, the stock is recovering from the US$3.1B AML fine and US asset cap imposed in late 2024. CEO Chun has called AML remediation the "number one priority," the US balance sheet restructuring is largely complete (10% asset reduction done), and EPS estimates have been revised up to C$8.86 for F2026 (+3%). The RSI at 60.5 reflects recovery momentum, not euphoria.

**Key Thesis Killer:** AML remediation takes longer or costs more than expected, or regulators impose additional restrictions. The US asset cap of US$434B constrains the growth runway for what was historically TD's primary growth engine.

**Verdict: Asymmetric Opportunity (60%)** -- The AML overhang has depressed TD's valuation relative to peers, creating a discount that should narrow as remediation milestones are hit through 2026. The ~4-5% dividend yield provides downside protection. The risk is binary: successful remediation unlocks significant re-rating; failure to meet regulatory timelines could trigger further penalties.

---

#### 11. BMO.TO -- Bank of Montreal (CAD 199.76) | **Wait & See -- 45%**

**Dip Analysis:** BMO reports Q1 2026 on Feb 25 with consensus EPS of C$3.23. The bank posted record FY2025 net income of C$9.2B with 26% EPS growth, driven by the Bank of the West integration. However, the US segment still needs further balance sheet optimization per Morningstar. RSI at 67.2 is approaching overbought territory.

**Key Thesis Killer:** US segment integration risk. The Bank of the West acquisition brought significant scale but the optimization process is ongoing. If US credit quality deteriorates (rising US unemployment, CRE exposure), BMO's over-indexed US operations become a drag.

**Verdict: Wait & See (45%)** -- Strong momentum but RSI at 67 and unfinished US optimization argue for patience. Wait for a pullback to the C$180 range where the risk/reward improves.

---

#### 12. SU.TO -- Suncor Energy (CAD 76.23) | **Wait & See -- 50%**

**Dip Analysis:** Suncor achieved its three-year Investor Day targets one year early with record 2025 operational results. 2026 guidance is robust: 840-870K bbls/d production, 99-102% refinery utilization, C$3.3B in buybacks. The WTI breakeven has been cut to US$53/bbl. RSI at 66 is elevated. The operational turnaround under the current management team has been genuine and impressive.

**Key Thesis Killer:** A sustained oil price decline below US$55 WTI. While Suncor has structurally lowered its breakeven, oil sands operations carry high fixed costs. Sub-$55 WTI for multiple quarters would force capex cuts and threaten the buyback program.

**Verdict: Wait & See (50%)** -- Operationally the best it has ever been, but the stock reflects this. At C$76.23 with RSI 66, the market has priced in the turnaround. A pullback to C$65-68 on oil price weakness would create a better entry.

---

#### 13. CNQ.TO -- Canadian Natural Resources (CAD 58.00) | **Value Trap -- 55%**

**Dip Analysis:** CNQ is technically overbought at RSI 76.2, the highest on this entire list. Despite solid fundamentals -- record production of 1.62M BOE/d, 25 consecutive dividend increases, 5.4% yield -- the stock's recent 18.7% YTD rally has pushed it well above fair value. Analyst consensus price target averages only C$52.05, meaning the stock is trading ABOVE consensus targets by ~11%.

**Key Thesis Killer:** The stock is trading above analyst consensus targets at an RSI of 76.2. This is not a dip candidate -- it is a momentum trade at its apex. Any oil price correction or production miss will trigger a sharp mean reversion.

**Verdict: Value Trap (55%)** -- Excellent company, terrible entry point. The RSI screams overbought, and trading above consensus targets means the market has over-extrapolated the commodity rally. This is a sell-into-strength candidate, not a buy-the-dip candidate. Wait for C$48-50 range.

---

#### 14. MFC.TO -- Manulife Financial (CAD 50.16) | **Asymmetric Opportunity -- 60%**

**Dip Analysis:** Manulife shares fell 5% after Q4 2025 results despite posting C$1.5B in quarterly profit and hiking the dividend 10%. The sell-off was driven by softer Hong Kong sales and C$9.5B in net asset management outflows -- both cyclical headwinds, not structural impairments. New business CSM was up 25% in Q3 2025, proving the insurance franchise remains healthy. RSI at 46.5 is the lowest among all Canadian names on this list, suggesting genuine oversold conditions relative to peers.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Asset management outflows accelerate. If the C$9.5B quarterly outflow pattern continues, it signals deeper competitive problems in the WAM division, not just a one-off. Hong Kong sales softness, if persistent, removes a key growth lever.

**Verdict: Asymmetric Opportunity (60%)** -- The post-earnings sell-off on cyclical headwinds (HK sales, AM outflows) has created a rare entry point for a stock with strong core insurance fundamentals, 10% dividend growth, and a new buyback program. Among Canadian financials, MFC offers the best contrarian risk/reward at the lowest RSI reading.

---

#### 15. NTR.TO -- Nutrien (CAD 97.43) | **Asymmetric Opportunity -- 62%**

**Dip Analysis:** Nutrien is the only non-financial on this list and offers genuine sector diversification. Full-year 2025 profit hit C$2.3B, with 2026 guidance reflecting growth in upstream fertilizer volumes, higher retail earnings, and potash prices up ~20% YoY. The company expects a fourth consecutive year of global potash demand growth with tight fundamentals as demand tests global supply chain capacity. RSI at 57.7 is neutral.

**Key Thesis Killer:** Fertilizer price downcycle extension. While potash fundamentals are currently tight, phosphate faces challenges, and any global agricultural recession (trade wars, weather disruption) could collapse fertilizer demand. Nutrien's retail division (~40% of EBITDA) is also exposed to North American farm economics.

**Verdict: Asymmetric Opportunity (62%)** -- The highest-conviction name among the non-financials. Potash supply tightness is structural (limited new capacity globally), the 2026 guidance is conservative, and Nutrien is the world's largest potash producer with pricing power. At C$97.43 with a neutral RSI, this offers genuine dip-buying potential in a sector with favorable supply/demand dynamics. The Q4 miss creates a sentiment gap that fundamentals should close.

---

## Top Picks Summary

**If forced to pick the best opportunities right now:**

1. **ISP.MI (Intesa Sanpaolo) -- EUR 5.87** -- Best risk/reward in the entire list. Record profitability, 95% payout, neutral RSI, 10-23% upside to analyst targets. The Italian sovereign risk is the known bear case but is structurally mitigated.

2. **NTR.TO (Nutrien) -- CAD 97.43** -- Best non-financial opportunity. Structural potash supply tightness, rising prices, conservative guidance, neutral RSI. Provides genuine sector diversification away from the financial services concentration in this list.

3. **MFC.TO (Manulife) -- CAD 50.16** -- Best contrarian Canadian play. Post-earnings sell-off on cyclical (not structural) issues. Lowest RSI among Canadian names at 46.5.

4. **TD.TO (Toronto-Dominion) -- CAD 132.79** -- Highest-upside Canadian bank if AML remediation succeeds. Valuation discount to peers should narrow.

5. **REP.MC (Repsol) -- EUR 18.30** -- Best energy play with 6.6% yield floor and upstream IPO catalyst, though RSI overbought argues for a small pullback before entry.

**Avoid:** CNQ.TO at RSI 76.2 trading above consensus targets -- this is not a dip, it is a momentum peak.
